Start with a phrase, a line, a quote. Questions are very helpful. Begin with a few you&#8217;re carrying right now.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Everything-Comes-Next-Collected-Poems/dp/0063013452/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"418\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?fit=320%2C418&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Pleasure and Spaciousness: Poet Naomi Shihab Nye&#8217;s Advice on Writing, Discipline, and the Two Driving Forces of Creativity\" loading=\"lazy\" https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?resize=600%2C784&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?resize=240%2C314&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?resize=768%2C1003&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?resize=1176%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1176w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?resize=1568%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1568w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“A self-respecting artist must not fold his hands on the pretext that he is not in the mood,” Tchaikovsky wrote to his patron as he contemplated <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/07/24/tchaikovsky-on-work-ethic-vs-inspiration/\">the interplay of discipline and creativity</a>. A century later, James Baldwin echoed the sentiment in his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/02/08/james-baldwin-advice-on-writing/\">advice on writing</a>, observing: “Talent is insignificant. I know a lot of talented ruins. Beyond talent lie all the usual words: discipline, love, luck, but most of all, endurance.”</p>\n<p>But for those of us who show up to do what we do day after day, inner rain or shine, as the days unspool into years &#8212; <em>Brain Pickings</em> turns 15 this year &#8212; there is something more than white-knuckle discipline making the steadfast labor not only bearable, not only sustainable, but vitalizing, inspiriting, joyful. What fuels the engine of endurance is a passionate enchantment &#8212; something of which Baldwin&#8217;s &#8220;love&#8221; reflects a glimmer but does not fully capture. </p>\n<p>The most marvelous part of it is this: It is an enchantment we cast upon ourselves.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72916\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642772_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=680%2C801&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"801\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72916\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=320%2C377&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=600%2C707&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=240%2C283&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=768%2C905&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/09/dorothy-lathrop-down-adown-derry/\">Dorothy Lathrop</a>, 1922. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642772_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642772_cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>How to cast that enchantment and how to couple it with the requisite endurance is what Your People&#8217;s Poet Laureate <strong>Naomi Shihab Nye</strong>, composer of the existentially symphonic <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/04/01/naomi-shihab-nye-kindness-animated/\">&#8220;Kindness,&#8221;</a> explores in a short, splendid prose reflection tucked into the final pages of her altogether soul-broadening collection <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Everything-Comes-Next-Collected-Poems/dp/0063013452/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Everything Comes Next: Collected and New Poems</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/everything-comes-next-collected-new-poems/oclc/1256002891&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>).</p>\n<p>In a sentiment evocative of Bertrand Russell&#8217;s lovely notion of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/05/13/bertrand-russell-mysticism-logic-time/\">&#8220;largeness of contemplation&#8221;</a> in calibrating the relationship between intuition and the intellect, Nye writes:  </p>\n<blockquote><p>Two helpful words to keep in mind at the beginning of any writing adventure are pleasure and spaciousness. If we connect a sense of joy with our writing, we may be inclined to explore further. What&#8217;s there to find out? Perhaps too much stock has been placed in big ideas or even small ones &#8212; a myth! &#8212; but regularity seems like a key. Don&#8217;t start with a big idea. Start with a phrase, a line, a quote. Questions are very helpful. Begin with a few you&#8217;re carrying right now.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In consonance with John Steinbeck&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/02/john-steinbeck-working-days/\">life-tested, Nobel-earning conviction</a> that &#8220;in writing, habit seems to be a much stronger force than either willpower or inspiration,&#8221; she adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Small increments of writing time may matter more than we could guess. One thing leads to many &#8212; swerving off, linking up, opening of voices and images and memories. Nearby notebooks &#8212; or iPads or tablets or laptops &#8212; are surely helpful.</p></blockquote>\n<p>With this, Nye turns to the ongoing dialogue between the magic of creation and the mechanics of discipline:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Make a plan, and return to it. It&#8217;s a party to which we keep inviting ourselves.</p>\n<p>And we have so many realms of material that are very close by:</p>\n<p>Families<br />\nNeighborhoods<br />\nChanges<br />\nMemories<br />\nSpoken language woven into poems &#8212; something someone said to you a long time ago and you still remember it &#8212; why, out of all the talk, do you remember that thing?<br />\nPets<br />\nLosses<br />\nFirst Times<br />\nLast Times<br />\nFears<br />\nFriends<br />\nBeing Sick, Being Well<br />\nWhat we see out our windows<br />\nGifts<br />\nHistory &#8212; what used to be in this very place where we are sitting now?</p>\n<p>Start anywhere.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Although such constructed starting points might seem mechanistic, they are the lever that unlatches the expanse where the unexpected can begin to unfurl. That incubus where ideas collide with one another into <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/16/rilke-inspiration-creativity/\">the unconscious combinatorial process we call creativity</a> is also the place where the joy of all creative labor lives. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72914\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642738_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop6.jpg?resize=680%2C979&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"979\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72914\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop6.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop6.jpg?resize=320%2C461&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop6.jpg?resize=600%2C864&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop6.jpg?resize=240%2C346&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop6.jpg?resize=768%2C1106&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/09/dorothy-lathrop-down-adown-derry/\">Dorothy Lathrop</a>, 1922. Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642738_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642738_cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as stationery cards</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Returning to the twin consecrating forces of discipline, pleasure and spaciousness, Nye writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Spaciousness &#8212; any page is wider than it looks. You have no idea where this thing might be going. Write in nuggets &#8212; here are my questions, here are some details I saw within the last 24 hours, here are some quotes I heard people say today. Gather material first &#8212; then select and connect from it&#8230; Each thing gives us something else.</p>\n<p>The more any of us writes, the more our words will &#8220;come to us.&#8221; If we trust in the words and their own mysterious relationship with one another, they will help us find things out&#8230; Consider the pleasure we feel when we go to a beach. The broad beach, the bigger air, the endless swish of movement and backdrop of sound. We feel uplifted, exhilarated. Writing regularly can help us feel that way too.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64202\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/i-will-confront-these-shows-of-the-day-and-night_framed-print?sku=s6-8968158p21a12v52a13v54?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass19.jpg?resize=768%2C973&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1558\" class=\"size-full wp-image-64202\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Illustration by Margaret C. Cook for a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\">rare 1913 edition of <em>Leaves of Grass</em></a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/i-will-confront-these-shows-of-the-day-and-night_framed-print?sku=s6-8968158p21a12v52a13v54?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In a short poem from the same book, calling to mind poet Ross Gay&#8217;s reflection on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/14/ross-gay-delights-handwriting/\">writing by hand as an instrument of thought</a>, Nye considers the practical tools that carve out this observant spaciousness in which impressions can collide and coalesce into ideas:</p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>ALWAYS BRING A PENCIL</strong><br />\n<em>by Naomi Shihab Nye</em></p>\n<p>There will not be a test.<br />\nIt does not have to be<br />\na Number 2 pencil.</p>\n<p>But there will be certain things &#8212;<br />\nthe quiet flush of waves,<br />\nripe scent of fish,<br />\nsmooth ripple of the wind&#8217;s second name &#8212;<br />\nthat prefer to be written about<br />\nin pencil.</p>\n<p>It gives them more room<br />\nto move around.</p></blockquote>\n<p>For more practical and philosophical reflections on the craft from great poets, savor Mary Oliver&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/01/14/mary-oliver-advice-on-writing/\">advice on writing</a>, Elizabeth Alexander on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/05/24/elizabeth-alexander-power-and-possibility-writing/\">language as a vehicle for the poetry of personhood</a>, and Rilke on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/29/rilke-letters-to-a-young-poet-macy-barrows/\">the relationship between solitude, love, and creativity</a>, then revisit Rachel Carson on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/08/28/rachel-carson-house-of-life-writing-loneliness/\">the sacred loneliness of writing</a> and Walt Whitman on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/01/03/whitman-emerson-criticism/\">the discipline of creative self-esteem</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/everythingcomesnext_naomishihabnye.jpg?fit=320%2C418&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn80@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-32-137_088317018af67ab5.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=680%2C801&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn39@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-36-666_71e5e276e7515fbb.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop6.jpg?resize=680%2C979&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn47@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-35-34-667_222dbdfbcff56b02.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass19.jpg?resize=768%2C973&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn7@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-33-859_f1e8f393e27cde9d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/-wbcwPCn4R4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn60@2020_3/2021/07/12/18-35-34-683_6132dd5688d846b0.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114913560},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","title":"How Memory Makes Us and Breaks Truth: The Rashomon Effect and the Science of How Memories Form and Falter in the Brain","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73809","description":"<h3>&#8220;We are our memory… that chimerical museum of shifting shapes, that pile of broken mirrors.”</h3>\n<hr>\n<p>It is already disorienting enough to accept that our attention <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/08/12/on-looking-eleven-walks-with-expert-eyes/\">only absorbs a fraction</a> of the events and phenomena unfolding within and around us at any given moment. Now consider that our memory only retains a fraction of what we have attended to in moments past. In the act of recollection, we take these fragments of fragments and try to reconstruct from them a totality of a remembered reality, playing out in the theater of the mind &#8212; a stage on which, as neuroscientist Antonio Damasio has observed in his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/07/05/antonio-damasio-the-feeling-of-what-happens-mind-body/\">landmark work on consciousness</a>, we often &#8220;use our minds not to discover facts, but to hide them.&#8221;</p>\n<p>We do this on the personal level &#8212; out of such selective memory and by such exquisite exclusion, we compose the narrative that is <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/01/15/oliver-sacks-identity-self-narrative/\">the psychological pillar of our identity</a>. We do it on the cultural level &#8212; what we call history is a collective selective memory that excludes far more of the past&#8217;s realities than it includes. Borges captured this with his characteristic poetic-philosophical precision when he observed that &#8220;we are our memory&#8230; that chimerical museum of shifting shapes, that pile of broken mirrors.&#8221; To be aware of memory&#8217;s chimera is to recognize the slippery, shape-shifting nature of even those truths we think we are grasping most firmly. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/07/22/the-book-of-memory-gaps-cecilia-ruiz/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/thebookofmemorygaps_ceciliaruiz8.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Cecilia Ruiz from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/07/22/the-book-of-memory-gaps-cecilia-ruiz/\"><em>The Book of Memory Gaps</em></a>, inspired by Borges</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Nearly a century after Nietzsche admonished that what we call <em>truth</em> is <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/03/26/nietzsche-on-truth-and-lies-in-a-nonmoral-sense/\">&#8220;a movable host of metaphors, metonymies, and anthropomorphisms&#8230; a sum of human relations which have been poetically and rhetorically intensified, transferred, and embellished,&#8221;</a> the great Japanese filmmaker <strong>Akira Kurosawa</strong> (March 23, 1910&#8211;September 6, 1998) created an exquisite cinematic metaphor for the slippery memory-mediated nature of truth in his 1950 film <em>Rashomon</em>, based on Ryunosuke Akutagawa’s short story &#8220;In a Grove&#8221; &#8212; a psychological-philosophical thriller about the murder of a samurai and its four witnesses, who each recount a radically different reality, each equally believable, thus undermining our most elemental trust in truth. </p>\n<p>As researchers in the second half of the twentieth century came to shed light on the foibles of memory, Kurosawa&#8217;s masterpiece lent its name to the amply documented unreliability of eyewitness accounts. The Rashomon effect, detailed in this wonderful animated primer from <a href=\"https://ed.ted.com/lessons/can-you-trust-your-memory-sheila-marie-orfano\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TED-Ed</a>, casts a haunting broader nimbus of doubt over our basic grasp of reality &#8212; we only exist, after all, as eyewitnesses of our own lives.</p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"How do you know what&#039;s true? - Sheila Marie Orfano\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/xg5y6Ao7VE4?feature=oembed&#38;rel=0&#38;controls=0&#38;showinfo=0&#38;iv_load_policy=3\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>All of these psychological perplexities arise from the basic neurophysiological infrastructure of how memories form and falter in the brain &#8212; something the great neurologist Oliver Sacks explored in his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/12/23/the-lost-mariner-tess-martin-oliver-sacks/\">classic medical poetics of memory disorders</a>, and something South African biomedical scientist Catharine Young explores in another TED-Ed episode, animated by the prolific <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/blank-on-blank/\">Patrick Smith</a>:</p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"How memories form and how we lose them - Catharine Young\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/yOgAbKJGrTA?feature=oembed&#38;rel=0&#38;controls=0&#38;showinfo=0&#38;iv_load_policy=3\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Complement with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/07/05/antonio-damasio-the-feeling-of-what-happens-mind-body/\"><em>Neurocomic</em></a> &#8212; a graphic novel about how the mind works &#8212; and the animated science of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/01/29/music-brain-ted-ed/\">how playing music benefits your brain more than any other activity</a>, then revisit Virginia Woolf on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/26/virginia-woolf-orlando-memory/\">how memory seams our lives</a>, Sally Mann on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/11/29/hold-still-sally-mann-memory/\">how photographs can unseam memory</a>, and neuroscientist Suzanne Corkin on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/06/08/permanent-present-tense-suzanne-corkin-h-m/\">how medicine&#8217;s most famous amnesiac illuminates the wonders of consciousness</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>. Like? <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/newsletter/\">Sign up.</a></p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/77I7eB_-0lU\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 29 Jun 2021 15:26:29 +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/thebookofmemorygaps_ceciliaruiz8.jpg","linkMd5":"2996e037ad3d543808b998e9069f5897","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn51@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-35-31-968_ec8672b4b6d1736b.webp","destWidth":600,"destHeight":375,"sourceBytes":41504,"destBytes":41504,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/thebookofmemorygaps_ceciliaruiz8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn51@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-35-31-968_ec8672b4b6d1736b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/77I7eB_-0lU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn96@2020_3/2021/07/12/18-35-33-650_f22f98d7aabbd573.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114913544},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","title":"Perfect Flowers: Adventures in Nature’s Nonbinary Botany, with a Side of Emily Dickinson","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73816","description":"<h3>Rewilding the landscape of possibility for the poetry of being.</h3>\n<hr>\n<p>“In each of us two powers preside, one male, one female,&#8221; Virginia Woolf wrote in 1929, epochs before we had our ever-expanding twenty-first-century vocabulary of identities, as she <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/04/15/virginia-woolf-androgynous-mind/\">celebrated the &#8220;androgynous mind&#8221;</a> as the mind most &#8220;resonant and porous&#8230; naturally creative, incandescent and undivided.&#8221; Given Woolf arrived at <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/09/09/virginia-woolf-cotton-wool-moments-of-being/\">her exquisite epiphany about what it means to be an artist</a> while walking amid her blooming garden, she might have been pleased to know that the botanical term for the blossoms of androgenous plants, also known as bisexual plants &#8212; plants that contain both the male pollen-producing stamen and the female ovule-producing pistils, and can therefore self-pollinate &#8212; is <em>perfect flowers</em>.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73820\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/lily-from-flora-von-deutschland-1903_print?sku=s6-20912068p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/thome_lily_small.jpg?resize=680%2C1053&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1053\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73820\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/thome_lily_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/thome_lily_small.jpg?resize=320%2C496&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/thome_lily_small.jpg?resize=600%2C930&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/thome_lily_small.jpg?resize=240%2C372&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/thome_lily_small.jpg?resize=768%2C1190&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/thome_lily_small.jpg?resize=992%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 992w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Lily from <em>Flora von Deutschland</em>, 1903. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/lily-from-flora-von-deutschland-1903_print?sku=s6-20912068p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Among the most common perfect flowers are lilies, roses, irises, snapdragons, flax flowers, morning glories, petunias, and the flowers of the coffee plant, the apple tree, and the tomato (which was once known as <em>love apple</em>).</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_69844\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/tomato-by-elizabeth-blackwell-from-a-curious-herbal-1737-benefiting-the-nature-conservancy_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_tomato.jpg?resize=680%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1001\" class=\"size-full wp-image-69844\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_tomato.jpg?w=1411&#38;ssl=1 1411w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_tomato.jpg?resize=240%2C353&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_tomato.jpg?resize=320%2C471&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_tomato.jpg?resize=768%2C1131&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_tomato.jpg?resize=600%2C884&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_tomato.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Tomato, or Love-Apple, from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/29/elizabeth-blackwell-curious-herbal/\"><em>A Curious Herbal</em></a> &#8212; the illustrated encyclopedia of medicinal plants, which the young Elizabeth Blackwell published in 1737 to bail her husband out of debtor&#8217;s prison. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/tomato-by-elizabeth-blackwell-from-a-curious-herbal-1737-benefiting-the-nature-conservancy_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Plants that contain only one set of gametes &#8212; among them begonias, squash, asparagus, and cottonwood &#8212; are termed <em>imperfect</em>. Curiously, there are sets of seemingly similar species that fall into opposite categories: the almond tree blooms a perfect flower (which inspired <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/12/28/albert-camus-almond-trees-character/\">literature&#8217;s lushest metaphor for strength of character</a>), while the walnut and the hazelnut do not; soy is perfect, while corn is not. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73821\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/coffee-plant-by-etienne-denisse-from-flore-damerique-18435460716_print?sku=s6-20913509p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/coffea_small.jpg?resize=680%2C891&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"891\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73821\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/coffea_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/coffea_small.jpg?resize=320%2C419&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/coffea_small.jpg?resize=600%2C787&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/coffea_small.jpg?resize=240%2C315&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/coffea_small.jpg?resize=768%2C1007&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/coffea_small.jpg?resize=1172%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1172w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Coffee plant by Étienne Denisse from <em>Flore d&#8217;Amérique,</em> 1843. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/coffee-plant-by-etienne-denisse-from-flore-damerique-18435460716_print?sku=s6-20913509p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In one sense, perfect flowers are less evolutionarily helpless, not having to rely solely on pollinators to deliver the essential fertilizing material from another plant&#8217;s gene pool. But they are also more vulnerable &#8212; a single disease can vanquish a species with a self-contained gene pool, while a cross-pollinated plant is more likely to contain genes susceptible to the disease as well as genes resistant to it. Lest we forget, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/02/the-snail-with-the-right-heart/\">diversity is the wellspring of resilience</a> &#8212; in the evolution of nature, as in the ever-evolving conservatory of human nature we call society.  </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/02/the-snail-with-the-right-heart/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/snailwiththerightheart.jpg?resize=680%2C340&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"340\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-73818\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/snailwiththerightheart.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/snailwiththerightheart.jpg?resize=320%2C160&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/snailwiththerightheart.jpg?resize=600%2C300&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/snailwiththerightheart.jpg?resize=240%2C120&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/snailwiththerightheart.jpg?resize=768%2C384&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Ping Zhu from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/02/the-snail-with-the-right-heart/\"><em>The Snail with the Right Heart: A True Story</em></a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>“It has always pleased me to exalt plants in the scale of organised beings,” Charles Darwin wrote in his autobiography. Long before he developed his theory of evolution, his grandfather &#8212; the physician, poet, slave-trade abolitionist, and scientist-predating-<a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/10/20/mary-somerville/\">the-coining-of-<em>scientist</em></a> Erasmus Darwin &#8212; composed a book-length poem titled <em>The Botanic Garden</em>, using scientifically accurate poetry to enchant the popular imagination with the scandalous new science of sexual reproduction in plants. Published in 1791, the wildly popular book was deemed too explicit for unmarried women to read. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_69837\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/golden-flower-de-luce-by-elizabeth-blackwell-from-a-curious-herbal-1737_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_iris.jpg?resize=680%2C1031&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1031\" class=\"size-full wp-image-69837\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_iris.jpg?w=1383&#38;ssl=1 1383w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_iris.jpg?resize=240%2C364&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_iris.jpg?resize=320%2C485&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_iris.jpg?resize=768%2C1164&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_iris.jpg?resize=600%2C910&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Iris from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/29/elizabeth-blackwell-curious-herbal/\"><em>A Curious Herbal</em></a> by Elizabeth Blackwell, 1737. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/golden-flower-de-luce-by-elizabeth-blackwell-from-a-curious-herbal-1737_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Half a century after <em>The Botanic Garden</em>, the young Emily Dickinson, who was a gardener before she was a poet, approached this dual reverence of the botanical and the poetic from a different angle in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/23/emily-dickinson-herbarium/\">her herbarium</a> &#8212; a meticulously composed collection of 424 New England wildflowers, including hundreds of perfect flowers, arranged with a stunning sensitivity to scale and visual cadence across the pages of the large album, with slim paper labels punctuating the specimens like enormous dashes inscribed with the names of the plants, sometimes the common and sometimes the Linnaean. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/23/emily-dickinson-herbarium/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson_herbarium8.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Page from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/23/emily-dickinson-herbarium/\">Emily Dickinson&#8217;s herbarium</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The herbarium was Emily Dickinson&#8217;s first formal work of composition, each flower a stanza in the poetry of landscape and life, deliberately placed to radiate a particular feeling-tone. Her poems were never published in book form in her lifetime, but this book of flowers remained with her and now survives her. </p>\n<p>On the cover of the first edition of her posthumously published poetry is a painting of one of her favorite wildflowers &#8212; the perfect flower <em>Monotropa uniflora</em>, commonly known as Indian Pipe for its shape when in bloom, or Ghost Flower for its lack of chlorophyll, which she considered &#8220;the preferred flower of life.&#8221; Once pollinated, the translucent white plant turns dark and dries up before releasing its resilient seeds into the living world.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73819\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/emilydickinson_poems_1890.jpg?resize=680%2C975&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"975\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73819\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/emilydickinson_poems_1890.jpg?w=785&#38;ssl=1 785w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/emilydickinson_poems_1890.jpg?resize=320%2C459&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/emilydickinson_poems_1890.jpg?resize=600%2C861&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/emilydickinson_poems_1890.jpg?resize=240%2C344&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/emilydickinson_poems_1890.jpg?resize=768%2C1102&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cover of the first edition of Emily Dickinson&#8217;s poems, 1890, featuring a painting of Indian Pipes by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/08/09/mabel-loomis-todd-total-eclipses-of-the-sun/\">Mabel Loomis Todd</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>When Emily Dickinson died at fifty-five, without a single white in her dark auburn hair, Susan &#8212; <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/12/10/emily-dickinson-love-letters-susan-gilbert/\">the great love of her life</a> &#8212; wrapped her in a white robe and rested alongside her in the small white casket a single pink lady’s slipper &#8212; a rare orchid associated with Venus, beautiful and savage, a living Georgia O’Keeffe painting. Into the neck of the white shroud she tucked a small posy of violets &#8212; the flower Emily cherished above all others for its “unsuspected” splendor, to which she had dedicated the most dramatic page of her herbarium. “Still in her Eye / The Violets lie,” she had written in one of her earliest and most intense poems dedicated to Sue, which ends with the declamation “Sue &#8212; forevermore!”</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/23/emily-dickinson-herbarium/\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson_herbarium36_violets.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Violets from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/23/emily-dickinson-herbarium/\">Emily Dickinson&#8217;s herbarium</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Living when she lived and loving whom she loved, in an imperfect world too small for her genius or her love, Emily Dickinson dreamt of lusher landscapes of possibility, leaping beyond her biology and the limiting binaries of her culture with her bold, subversive verses:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Amputate my freckled Bosom!<br />\nMake me bearded like a Man!</p></blockquote>\n<p>She never lived to see the human world live up to nature&#8217;s nonbinary botany of desire. </p>\n<p>But she had her love and all the perfect flowers.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. Quite.&#8221; </h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Darling-Baby-Maira-Kalman/dp/0316330620/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"363\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?fit=320%2C363&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover-landscape alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Darling Baby: Artist Maira Kalman&#8217;s Painted Serenade to Attention, Aliveness, and the Vibrancy of Seeing the World with Newborn Eyes\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?w=2259&#38;ssl=1 2259w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?resize=320%2C363&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?resize=600%2C680&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?resize=240%2C272&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?resize=768%2C870&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?resize=1355%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1355w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?resize=1807%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1807w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_kalman-scaled.jpg?w=2040&#38;ssl=1 2040w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>&#8220;The secret of success,&#8221; Jackson Pollock&#8217;s father wrote to the teenage artist-to-be in his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/02/02/jackson-pollock-father-letter/\">wonderful letter of life-advice</a>, &#8220;is to be fully awake to everything about you.” Few things beckon our attention and awaken us to life more compellingly than color. &#8220;Our lives, when we pay attention to light, compel us to empathy with color,&#8221; Ellen Meloy wrote in her exquisite <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/02/ellen-meloy-anthropology-of-turquioise/\">meditation on the chemistry, culture, and the conscience of color</a>. And why else live if not to pay attention to the changing light?</p>\n<p>In <strong><em><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Darling-Baby-Maira-Kalman/dp/0316330620/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Darling Baby</a></em></strong> (<em><a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/darling-baby/oclc/1152424409&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">public library</a></em>), artist <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/maira-kalman/\">Maira Kalman</a>, a poet of chromatic tenderness, composes an uncommon ode to aliveness, to the vibrant beauty of life, life that is very new and life that is very old.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Darling-Baby-Maira-Kalman/dp/0316330620/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img /></a></p>\n<p>As she teaches the baby to look at this color, this shape, this quality of light, we see the grownup relearn to see with those baby-eyes that are awake to the luminous everythingness of everything, undulled by the accumulation of filters we call growing up. What emerges is a celebration of attention as affirmation of aliveness, a vibrant testament to Simone Weil&#8217;s exquisite observation that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/08/19/simone-weil-attention-gravity-and-grace/\">&#8220;attention is the rarest and purest form of generosity.&#8221;</a> Page after painted page, a generous presence unfolds &#8212; presence with the new life of this small helpless observer of the world, presence with the ancient life of sky and sea.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Darling-Baby-Maira-Kalman/dp/0316330620/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" I think that is a good thing. At any rate, it is a thing.<br />\nI am telling you this because I know you will understand.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Throughout the story, there are echoes of Kalman&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/10/29/beloved-dog-maira-kalman/\">love of dogs</a>, echoes of her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/07/30/maira-kalman-thinking-feeling-interview/\">love of walking</a>, echoes of her love of dance and her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/11/29/american-utopia-maira-kalman-david-byrne/\">lovely </a><a _466d555fc45745f5.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman7.jpg?resize=680%2C387&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn86@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-35-33-671_c2f7bc615d693578.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman29.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn24@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-35-35-078_7bf0f070979a5c14.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman23.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn51@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-34-675_3546b6c445667b21.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman4.jpg?resize=680%2C387&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn88@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-35-34-878_7f9173da4ace49d9.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman25.jpg?resize=680%2C445&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn82@2020_3/2021/07/12/18-35-33-676_8fb463ad03149d5b.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman28.jpg?resize=680%2C445&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn59@2020_3/2021/07/12/18-35-35-321_dca040d1073e7f33.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman10.jpg?resize=680%2C741&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn56@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-33-998_5d73eab56c4ee849.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/darlingbaby_mairakalman20.jpg?resize=680%2C439&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn71@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-34-008_963182dc85b88203.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/QlG9VuEpysg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn80@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-35-34-372_3a74c13d59d674f2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114913544},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","title":"Rilke on the Relationship Between Solitude, Love, Sex, and Creativity","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73803","description":"<h3>&#8220;There is only one solitude, and it is large and not easy to bear&#8230; People are drawn to the easy and to the easiest side of the easy. But it is clear that we must hold ourselves to the difficult.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Letters-Young-Poet-Translation-Commentary/dp/1611806860/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"512\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?fit=320%2C512&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Rilke on the Relationship Between Solitude, Love, Sex, and Creativity\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?w=1313&#38;ssl=1 1313w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?resize=320%2C512&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?resize=600%2C960&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?resize=240%2C384&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?resize=768%2C1228&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?resize=960%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 960w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/letterstoayoungpoet_rilke_macy_barrows.jpg?resize=1280%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1280w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“You are born alone. You die alone. The value of the space in between is trust and love,” artist Louise Bourgeois wrote in her diary in her seventy-seventh year as she looked back on a long and lush life to consider <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/04/15/louise-bourgeois-solitude/\">the central role of solitude in creativity</a>.</p>\n<p>A generation before her, recognizing that &#8220;works of art arise from an infinite aloneness,&#8221; <strong>Rainer Maria Rilke</strong> (December 4, 1875&#8211;December 29, 1926) explored the relationship between solitude, love, and creativity in his stunning correspondence with the nineteen-year-old Franz Xaver Kappus &#8212; an aspiring poet and cadet at the same military academy that had <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/03/29/rilke-letters-teacher/\">nearly broken Rilke&#8217;s own adolescent soul</a>.</p>\n<p>Posthumously published in German, these letters of uncommonly penetrating insight into the essence of art and love &#8212; that is, the essence of life &#8212; now come alive afresh as <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Letters-Young-Poet-Translation-Commentary/dp/1611806860/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Letters to a Young Poet: A New Translation and Commentary</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/letters-to-a-young-poet-a-new-translation-and-commentary/oclc/1249108979?referer=br&#038;ht=edition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) by ecological philosopher, Buddhist scholar, and environmental activist Joanna Macy, and poet and clinical psychologist Anita Barrows: two women who have lived into the far reaches of life &#8212; Macy was ninety-one at the time of the translation and Barrows seventy-three &#8212; and who have spent a quarter century <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/12/10/joanna-macy-a-year-with-rilke-death-mortality/\">thinking deeply about what makes life worth living</a> in translating together the works of a long-ago man who barely survived to fifty and who was still in his twenties when he composed these letters of tender and timeless lucidity.</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Letters-Young-Poet-Translation-Commentary/dp/1611806860/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/rilke4.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\"></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">1902 portrait of Rilke by his brother-in-law, Helmuth Westhoff</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Anticipating the illuminations of twentieth-century psychology about why a childhood capacity for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/07/18/adam-phillips-on-risk-and-solitude/\">&#8220;fertile solitude&#8221; </a> is essential for creativity, self-esteem, and healthy relationships later in life, Rilke writes to his young correspondent in the short, dark, lonesome days just before the winter holidays:</p>\n<blockquote><p>What (you might ask yourself) would a solitude be that didn’t have some greatness to it? For there is only one solitude, and it is large and not easy to bear. It comes almost all the time when you’d gladly exchange it for any togetherness, however banal and cheap; exchange it for the appearance of however strong a conformity with the ordinary, with the least worthy. But perhaps that is precisely the time when solitude ripens; its ripening can be painful as the growth of a boy and sad like the beginning of spring&#8230; What is needed is only this: solitude, great inner solitude. Going within and meeting no one else for hours &#8212; that is what one must learn to attain. To be solitary as one was as a child. As the grown-ups were moving about, preoccupied with things that seemed big and important because the grown-ups appeared so busy and because you couldn’t understand what they were doing.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/07/25/ruth-krauss-maurice-sendak-open-house-for-butterflies/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/openhouseforbutterflies18.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Illustration by Maurice Sendak from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/07/25/ruth-krauss-maurice-sendak-open-house-for-butterflies/\"><em>Open House for Butterflies</em></a> by Ruth Krauss.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Echoing Kierkegaard&#8217;s ever-timely insistence that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/05/05/kierkegaard-on-presence-unhappiness/\">&#8220;of all ridiculous things the most ridiculous seems&#8230; to be busy&#8221;</a> and Emerson&#8217;s observation that &#8220;our hurry &#038; embarrassment look ridiculous&#8221; the moment we pause <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/02/28/emerson-journals-surfaces/\">the headlong rush of sociality through which we try to escape from ourselves</a>, Rilke adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>If one day one grasps that their busyness is pathetic, their occupations frozen and disconnected from life, why then not continue to see like a child, see it as strange, see it out of the depth of one’s own world, the vastness of one’s own solitude, which is, in itself, work and status and vocation?</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_66748\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/solitude-by-maria-popova_print?sku=s6-11544229p4a1v2?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Solitude-by-Maria-Popova.jpg?resize=680%2C907&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"907\" class=\"size-full wp-image-66748\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Solitude-by-Maria-Popova.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Solitude-by-Maria-Popova.jpg?resize=240%2C320&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Solitude-by-Maria-Popova.jpg?resize=320%2C427&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Solitude-by-Maria-Popova.jpg?resize=768%2C1024&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Solitude-by-Maria-Popova.jpg?resize=600%2C800&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">&#8220;Solitude&#8221; by Maria Popova. Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/solitude-by-maria-popova_print?sku=s6-11544229p4a1v2?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>And yet the crucial, exquisite creative tension that Rilke so singularly harmonizes is the essential interplay between solitude and love &#8212; each enriching the other, each magnifying the totality of the spirit from which all art springs. In another letter penned the following spring, he writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Don’t let your solitude obscure the presence of something within it that wants to emerge. Precisely this presence will help your solitude expand. People are drawn to the easy and to the easiest side of the easy. But it is clear that we must hold ourselves to the difficult, as is true for everything alive. Everything in nature grows and defends itself in its own way and against all opposition, straining from within and at any price to become distinctively itself. It is good to be solitary, because solitude is difficult, and that a thing is difficult must be even more of a reason for us to undertake it.</p>\n<p>To love is good too, for love is difficult. For one person to care for another, that is perhaps the most difficult thing required of us, the utmost and final test, the work for which all other work is but a preparation. With our whole being, with all the strength we have gathered, we must learn to love. This learning is ever a committed and enduring process.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64208\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/how-calm-how-solemn-it-grows-to-ascend-the-atmosphere-of-lovers_print?sku=s6-8967910p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=680%2C899&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"899\" class=\"size-full wp-image-64208\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=240%2C317&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=320%2C423&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=768%2C1015&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=600%2C793&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Margaret C. Cook from a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\">rare 1913 edition</a> of Walt Whitman&#8217;s <em>Leaves of Grass</em>. Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/how-calm-how-solemn-it-grows-to-ascend-the-atmosphere-of-lovers_print?sku=s6-8967910p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Two decades before Kahlil Gibran offered his abiding poetic wisdom on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/27/kahlil-gibran-the-prophet-love-marriage/\">the difficult balance of intimacy and independence in true love</a>, Rilke calls for shedding the ideological shackles of our culture&#8217;s conception of love as a melding of entities. &#8220;No human experience is so rife with conventions as this,&#8221; he observes with an eye to those who have not yet befriended their sovereign solitude and instead &#8220;act from mutual helplessness&#8221; to &#8220;simply surrender to love as an escape from loneliness.&#8221; He offers the liberating alternative that still requires as much countercultural courage in our day as it did in his:</p>\n<blockquote><p>To love is not about merging. It is a noble calling for the individual to ripen, to differentiate, to become a world in oneself in response to another. It is a great, immodest call that singles out a person and summons them beyond all boundaries. Only in this sense may we use the love that has been given us. This is humanity’s task, for which we are still barely ready.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>This more human love (endlessly considerate and light and good and clear, consummated by holding close and letting go) will resemble that love that we so arduously prepare &#8212; the love that consists of two solitudes that protect, border, and greet each other.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64219\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass17.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1543\" class=\"size-full wp-image-64219\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Margaret C. Cook for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\"><em>Leaves of Grass</em></a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/thoughts-silent-thoughts-of-time-and-space-and-death_framed-print?sku=s6-8967472p21a12v52a13v54?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In another letter, Rilke adds the complexity of physical intimacy to this realm of transcendent difficulty, formulating his advice on how to best harness eros as a creative force:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Yes, sex is hard. But anything expected of us is hard. Almost everything that matters is hard, and everything matters&#8230; Come to your own relationship to sex, free of custom and convention. Then you need not fear to lose yourself and become unworthy of your better nature.</p>\n<p>Sexual pleasure is a sensory experience, no different from pure seeing or pure touch, like the taste of a fruit. It is a great, endless experience given to us, a natural part of knowing our world, of the fullness and brilliance of every knowing. And nothing we receive is wrong. What’s wrong is to misuse and spoil this experience and to use it to excite the exhausted aspects of our lives, to dissipate rather than connect.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Long before scientists shed light on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/07/14/bumbebees-glouson/\">how the sexuality of early flora and fauna gave our planet its beauty</a>, Rilke adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Seeing the beauty in animals and plants is a form of love and longing; and we can see the animal, as we see the plant, patient and willing to come together and increase &#8212; not out of physical lust, not out of suffering, but bowing to necessities that are greater than lust and suffering and more powerful than will and resistance. </p>\n<p>Oh that humans might humbly receive and earnestly bear this mystery that fills the earth down to the smallest thing, and feel it as part of life’s travail, instead of taking it lightly. If they could only be respectful of this fertility, which is undivided, whether in spiritual or physical form. For this spiritual creativity stems from the physical, derives from that erotic essence, and is but an airier, more delightful, more eternal iteration of its lush sensuality.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_69840\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/red-poppy-by-elizabeth-blackwell-from-a-curious-herbal-1737-benefits-the-nature-conservancy_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_poppy.jpg?resize=680%2C986&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"986\" class=\"size-full wp-image-69840\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_poppy.jpg?w=1429&#38;ssl=1 1429w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_poppy.jpg?resize=240%2C348&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_poppy.jpg?resize=320%2C464&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_poppy.jpg?resize=768%2C1114&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_poppy.jpg?resize=600%2C870&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/elizabethblackwell_curiousherbal_poppy.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Red poppy from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/29/elizabeth-blackwell-curious-herbal/\"><em>A Curious Herbal</em></a> by Elizabeth Blackwell, 1737. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/red-poppy-by-elizabeth-blackwell-from-a-curious-herbal-1737-benefits-the-nature-conservancy_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>So too with the role of the erotic in creative work:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The art of creating is nothing without the vast ongoing participation and collaboration of the real world, nothing without the thousandfold harmonizing of things and beings; and the creator’s pleasure is thereby inexpressibly rich because it contains memories of the begetting and bearing of millions. In a single creative thought dwell a thousand forgotten nights of love, which infuse it with immensity. And those who come together in the night, locked in thrusting desire, are gathering nectar, generating power and sweetness for some future poetic utterance that will sing the rapture.</p></blockquote>\n<p>For more of and about this ravishing new translation of <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Letters-Young-Poet-Translation-Commentary/dp/1611806860/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Letters to a Young Poet</em></strong></a> &#8212; one which embodies the Nobel-winning Polish poet Wisława Szymborska’s notion of “that rare miracle when a translation stops being a translation and becomes&#8230; a second original,” and the finest such miracle performed on a classic since Ursula K. Le Guin&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/10/21/lao-tzu-tao-te-ching-ursula-k-le-guin/\">feminist translation of the <em>Tao Te Ching</em></a> &#8212; savor this <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/programs/joanna-macy-and-anita-barrows-what-a-world-youve-got-inside-you/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>On Being</em> conversation</a> with Macy and Barrows about the wider resonances of Rilke&#8217;s work in our world, then revisit Rilke&#8217;s contemporary Hermann Hesse on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/01/15/hermann-hesse-solitude-suffering-destiny/\">solitude and the courage to find yourself</a>, physicist Brian Greene&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/25/brian-greene-rilke/\">Rilkean reflection on how to live with our human vulnerabilities</a>, and Rilke himself on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/10/04/rilke-letters-to-a-young-poet-writing/\">what it takes to be an artist</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter.
