02:35:13","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","title":"From Cacao to Clitoria: Luscious 19th-Century French Botanical Illustrations of the Most Vibrant Flora of the Americas","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73854","description":"<h3>How the world relished the world before Instagram. </h3> \n<hr> \n <p>To put our familiar lives in perspective and jolt us awake to the wonder of so much we have come to take for granted, let us picture this:</p> \n <p>It is the 1840s and you, like most of humanity, have never traveled more than a few miles beyond where you were born, have never met a person native to a different country, have never seen a bird native to a different continent or a flower native to a different climate. Like most of humanity, you never will. Photography <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/04/03/virginia-woolf-julia-margaret-cameron-photography/\">has just been born</a>, too costly and cumbersome a technology to carry into the world, much less to carry the world to you. If you have had the privilege of setting foot in a library — that is, if you were born with a Y chromosome and very little melanin — you might have leafed through a heavy leather-bound encyclopedia or <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/23/emily-dickinson-herbarium/\">an herbarium</a> and marveled at <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/11/18/george-edwards-gleanings-natural-history/\">life-forms from faraway lands</a>. If you are among the slender portion of our species lucky enough to live near one of the world’s handful of natural history museums and botanical gardens, you might have glimpsed some specimens of exotic plants. </p> \n <p>But you are you — whatever degree of privilege chance has conferred upon you at birth, you are curious and you hunger for beauty, enraptured by the artwork that is your only portal to the living wonders of this world.</p> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73872\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/passionflower-and-passionfruit-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s5493885_print?sku=s6-20994388p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_passionfruit_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C964&amp;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"964\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73872\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_passionfruit_sm.jpg?w=1200&amp;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_passionfruit_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C454&amp;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_passionfruit_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C851&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_passionfruit_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C340&amp;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_passionfruit_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C1089&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_passionfruit_sm.jpg?resize=1084%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 1084w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>\n  <figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n   Passionflower and passionfruit. (Available as \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/passionflower-and-passionfruit-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s5493885_print?sku=s6-20994388p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, a \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cutting-boards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cutting board</a>, and \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, benefitting the New York Botanical Garden.)\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <p>Before science made the technologies of image-capture and global travel possible, botanical and natural history illustrators were singular civil servants — artists in the service of their subjects, tasked with capturing and conveying what it is like to be a particular plant or animal living in a particular habitat. <em>Here,</em> each exquisitely rendered specimen seems to say to its remote viewer, <em>aren’t I strange and beautiful and worthy of inclusion in the family of life?</em></p> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73874\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/chirimuya-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s_print?sku=s6-20994466p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_-chirimuya_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C931&amp;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"931\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73874\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_-chirimuya_sm.jpg?w=1200&amp;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_-chirimuya_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C438&amp;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_-chirimuya_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C822&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_-chirimuya_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C329&amp;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_-chirimuya_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C1052&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_-chirimuya_sm.jpg?resize=1122%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 1122w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>\n  <figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n   Chirimuya. (Available as \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/chirimuya-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s_print?sku=s6-20994466p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, a \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cutting-boards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cutting board</a>, and \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, benefitting the New York Botanical Garden.)\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <p>Few artists have accomplished this more effectively and enchantingly than <strong>Étienne Denisse</strong> (1785–1861). </p> \n <p>As a young artist at the botanical garden of the natural history museum in Paris, Denisse had attracted the attention of the crown with his uncommonly detailed and scrumptious paintings of plants. He was eventually hired as lithographer for the French royal court, then dispatched to the French Caribbean territories, where he spent many years collecting and studying plants completely novel to European eyes, periodically sending his illustrations back to France. Between 1843 and 1846, two hundred and one astonishing hand-colored lithographic plates based on Denisse’s drawings from life were published as <a href=\"https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/185335?utm_medium=social%20media&amp;utm_source=blogger&amp;utm_campaign=Book%20of%20the%20Month&amp;utm_content=NYBG#page/1/mode/1up\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Flore d’Amérique</em></strong></a>. One of the very few surviving copies has been painstakingly restored and digitized by the wonderland that is the <a href=\"https://www.nybg.org/learn/mertz-library/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">LuEsther T. Mertz Library</a> of the New York Botanical Garden in collaboration with the <a href=\"https://library.si.edu/donate/bhl-donation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Biodiversity Heritage Library</a>. </p> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73856\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s_print?sku=s6-20979488p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse1.jpg?resize=680%2C895&amp;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"895\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73856\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse1.jpg?w=1200&amp;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse1.jpg?resize=320%2C421&amp;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse1.jpg?resize=600%2C790&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse1.jpg?resize=240%2C316&amp;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse1.jpg?resize=768%2C1011&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse1.jpg?resize=1167%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 1167w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>\n  <figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n   Hiliconia. (Available as \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s_print?sku=s6-20979488p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, a \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cutting-boards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cutting board</a>, and \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, benefitting the New York Botanical Garden.)\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <p>Denisse did for the plants of the Americas what the Dutch engraver Louis Renard had done for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/08/15/louis-renard-poissons/\">the psychedelic fishes of the South Seas</a> a century earlier and what the English marine biologist William Saville Kent would do for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/11/william-saville-kent-great-barrier-reef-prints/\">the corals of the Great Barrier Reef</a> a generation later. Epochs before our digital voyeurism, before photo albums and air travel, his vibrant illustrations of unseen and unimaginable living wonders became the era’s <em>National Geographic</em> footage and Instagram feeds rolled into one. </p> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73871\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/mahogany-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s_print?sku=s6-20994338p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_mahogany_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C934&amp;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"934\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73871\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_mahogany_sm.jpg?w=1200&amp;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_mahogany_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C439&amp;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_mahogany_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C824&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_mahogany_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C330&amp;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_mahogany_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C1055&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_mahogany_sm.jpg?resize=1118%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 1118w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>\n  <figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n   Mahogany. (Available as \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/mahogany-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s_print?sku=s6-20994338p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, a \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cutting-boards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cutting board</a>, and \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, benefitting the New York Botanical Garden.)\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <p>Denisse seems to have had a special fondness for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/14/the-blue-hour-isabelle-simler/\">Earth’s very few true blues</a>. Blue-flowering plants, so rare in nature, occupy a sizable portion of his folios — among them the unexpected blossoms of the mahogany tree and the startling butterfly pea with its intensely colored cobalt flowers and their perfect bright-yellow folds that earned the plant the Latin name <em>Clitoria</em>. </p> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73880\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/clitoria-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s5493958_print?sku=s6-20994558p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/denisse_clitoria_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C921&amp;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"921\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73880\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/denisse_clitoria_sm.jpg?w=1200&amp;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/denisse_clitoria_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C434&amp;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/denisse_clitoria_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C813&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/denisse_clitoria_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C325&amp;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/denisse_clitoria_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C1041&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/denisse_clitoria_sm.jpg?resize=1134%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 1134w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>\n  <figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n   Clitoria, or butterfly pea. (Available as \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/clitoria-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s5493958_print?sku=s6-20994558p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, a \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cutting-boards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cutting board</a>, and \n   <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, benefitting the New York Botanical Garden.)\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73857\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73854/?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_celestine_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C1018&amp;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1018\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73857\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_celestine_sm.jpg?w=1200&amp;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_celestine_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C479&amp;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_celestine_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C898&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_celestine_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C359&amp;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_celestine_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C1149&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_celestine_sm.jpg?resize=1026%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 1026w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>\n  <figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n   Blue bindweed. </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <p>There are plants that are now fixtures of the global palate — the banana, mango, pineapple, cacao, coffee, coconut, various citrus fruit, and the avocado, that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/12/04/avocado-ghosts-of-evolution/\">gladsome ghost of evolution</a>. </p> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73863\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a strange plums; the blue flame of the Mexican verbena; the enticing evergreen flowering <em>Tillandsia</em>, which Denisse dubbed “the immortal Creole,” now teetering on the brink of ecological mortality; the scaly chirimuya fruit beloved by the Incas; the colossal thorned heart of its cousin the soursop, which I still remember first encountering in Kauai with gaping disbelief at the otherworldly life-forms of which this planet is capable; the mammoth gramophone blossom of the pelican flower, <em>Aristolochia grandiflora</em> — one of Earth’s largest flowers, with a scent of rotting flesh to attract flies as pollinators; the <em>Averrhoa</em> with its luscious striped fruit reminiscent of a mosque top, named after the 12th-century Islamic astronomer and philosopher Averroes. </p> \n <figure id=\"attachment_73858\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n  <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/averrhoa-from-flore-damerique-by-etienne-denisse-1840s_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_averrhoa_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C934&amp;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"934\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73858\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_averrhoa_sm.jpg?w=1200&amp;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_averrhoa_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C439&amp;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_averrhoa_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C824&amp;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_averrhoa_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C330&amp;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_averrhoa_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C1055&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/etiennedenisse_averrhoa_sm.jpg?resize=1118%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 1118w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>\n  <figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n   Averrhoa. Animated","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73898","description":"<h3>&#8220;A metaphor is language that simultaneously creates and solves its own riddle; within that minute explosion of mind is both expansion and release&#8230; It is how the mind instructs itself in a more complex seeing.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Ten-Windows-Great-Poems-Transform/dp/0345806840/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"450\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/tenwindows_hirshfield.jpg?fit=320%2C450&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"The Handle on the Door to a New World: Poet Jane Hirshfield on the Magic and Power of Metaphor, Animated\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/tenwindows_hirshfield.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/tenwindows_hirshfield.jpg?resize=240%2C338&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/tenwindows_hirshfield.jpg?resize=320%2C450&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/tenwindows_hirshfield.jpg?resize=768%2C1081&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/tenwindows_hirshfield.jpg?resize=600%2C845&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>It is a marvel, though hardly a surprise, that children&#8217;s minds are <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/08/19/james-geary-i-is-an-other-children-metaphor/\">machines for metaphor</a>. We are meaning-making creatures &#8212; from the moment we begin trying to make sense of the world, and even as we <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/11/01/alan-watts-wisdom-of-insecurity-3/\">face the terrifying prospect of its meaninglessness</a>, the familiar becomes our foothold for the unfamiliar; the images that already carry meaning, already invoke felt feeling-tones, become mirrors and magnifying glasses for those that don&#8217;t yet. Our entire experience of reality, bent through the lens of our meaning-hungry consciousness, becomes, as Nietzsche memorably put it, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/03/26/nietzsche-on-truth-and-lies-in-a-nonmoral-sense/\">&#8220;a movable host of metaphors, metonymies, and anthropomorphisms.&#8221;</a> Out of that moving host, the entire ecosystem of meaning we call art is born.</p>\n<p>That is what <strong>Jane Hirshfield</strong> &#8212; a poet capable of compressing <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/03/15/today-another-universe-jane-hirshfield-ledger-jasmine/\">a universe of meaning into a mouthful of words</a>, a thinker of uncommon insight into <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/07/21/jane-hirshfield-concentration/\">how language concentrates and consecrates reality</a>, and an ordained Buddhist whose contemplative practice animates her creative practice &#8212; explores in this lovely animated meditation on the magic of metaphor from my friends at <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/ted-ed/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TED-Ed</a>:</p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"The art of the metaphor - Jane Hirshfield\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/A0edKgL9EgM?feature=oembed&#38;rel=0&#38;controls=0&#38;showinfo=0&#38;iv_load_policy=3\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<blockquote><p>A good metaphor&#8230; is a way to let you feel and know something differently.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>Metaphors give words a way to go beyond their own meaning. They are handles on the door of what we can know and of what we can imagine. Each door leads to some new house and some new world that only that one handle can open. </p>\n<p>What&#8217;s amazing is this: By making a handle, you can make a world.</p></blockquote>\n<p>She takes up the subject throughout her book <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Ten-Windows-Great-Poems-Transform/dp/0345806840/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Ten Windows: How Great Poems Transform the World</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/ten-windows-how-great-poems-transform-the-world/oclc/950635295&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; which gave us her soulful meditation on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/10/02/jane-hirshfield-ten-windows-poetry/\">how art transforms us</a> &#8212; and writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Aristotle, in his <em>Rhetoric</em>, alludes to the kinship between metaphor and riddle, calling each a source for the other. Not only does solving a riddle depend on the ability to think metaphorically, all metaphor preserves some flavor of a puzzle. A metaphor is language that simultaneously creates and solves its own riddle; within that minute explosion of mind is both expansion and release. Perhaps this is why riddles abound among the earliest poems in many traditions and why spiritual teaching so often partakes of the riddling: it is how the mind instructs itself in a more complex seeing.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement with her short, splendid poems <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/14/jane-hirshfield-optimism-kelli-anderson-animation/\">&#8220;Optimism&#8221;</a> and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/23/the-weighing-jane-hirshfield/\">&#8220;The Weighing&#8221;</a> &#8212; both masterpieces of metaphor &#8212; then dwell with this <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/10/the-mirror-of-enigmas-borges-bloy/\">living metaphor for the riddle of life</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. Yes, there is joy, fulfillment and companionship — but the loneliness of the soul, in its appalling self-consciousness, is horrible and overpowering.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/The-Unabridged-Journals-Sylvia-Plath/dp/0385720254/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/06/sylviaplathjournals.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>Western psychologists have rightly observed that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/06/25/limbic-revision/\">&#8220;who we are and who we become depends, in part, on whom we love.&#8221;</a> Zen Buddhists have rightly observed that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/31/how-to-love-thich-nhat-hanh/\">&#8220;to love without knowing how to love wounds the person we love.&#8221;</a> That lacuna between <em>whom</em> and <em>how</em>, between the objects of our love and its observance, is powerful space for transformation. For those of us who have not come into the world under the most optimal of circumstances and have not been formed by the most nurturing of forces, relationships are especially fertile ground for growing the twin roots of the stable soul: love and trust. </p>\n<p>Yet always, always, there is an undertone of loneliness in even the most symphonic love &#8212; not the gladsome <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/09/03/rilke-love-marriage/\">&#8220;neighboring solitudes&#8221;</a> Rilke placed at the center of healthy companionship, but the hollowing loneliness of unbelonging, of never feeling fully and completely seen, which another great poet placed at the center of her poetry and her private anguish before she perished by that loneliness.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73502\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/sylviapalth_smithsonian.jpg?resize=680%2C908&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"908\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73502\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/sylviapalth_smithsonian.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Sylvia Plath by Rollie McKenna (Smithsonian National Portrait Gallery)</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Sylvia Plath</strong> (October 27, 1932&#8211;February 11, 1963) was still a teenager when she began facing the deepest existential questions, untangling them with uncommon lucidity on the pages of her diary, which now survive as <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/The-Unabridged-Journals-Sylvia-Plath/dp/0385720254/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>The Unabridged Journals of Sylvia Plath</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/unabridged-journals-of-sylvia-plath-1950-1962/oclc/44133088&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; the dazzling and at times discomposing posthumous echo of personhood that gave us the young Plath on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/06/12/sylvia-plath-journals-nature/\">finding nonreligious divinity in nature</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/06/18/sylvia-plath-journal/\">the ecsatsy of curiosity</a>, and her thoughts on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/02/11/sylvia-palth-on-life-death-hope-happiness/\">life, death, hope and happiness</a>.</p>\n<p>In an entry from the winter of her freshman year at Smith College, upon returning to her dorm room after a four-day blur with her family for Thanksgiving, she writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Now I know what loneliness is, I think. Momentary loneliness, anyway. It comes from a vague core of the self &#8212; like a disease of the blood, dispersed throughout the body so that one cannot locate the matrix, the spot of contagion. </p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>This loneliness will blur and diminish, no doubt, when tomorrow I plunge again into classes, into the necessity of studying for exams. But now, that false purpose is lifted and I am spinning in a temporary vacuum&#8230; The routine is momentarily suspended and I am lost. There is no living being on earth at this moment except myself. I could walk down the halls, and empty rooms would yawn mockingly at me from every side.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Peering beyond the immediate situation, beyond this particular moment in life, she casts a darkly prognostic eye toward the rosary of moments stringing her uncertain future &#8212; a future that would soon include <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/02/25/sylvia-plath-meets-ted-hughes/\">a passionate but damaging love</a>, a future cut short by her lonely pain &#8212; and adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>God, but life is loneliness, despite all the opiates, despite the shrill tinsel gaiety of “parties” with no purpose, despite the false grinning faces we all wear. And when at last you find someone to whom you feel you can pour out your soul, you stop in shock at the words you utter &#8212; they are so rusty, so ugly, so meaningless and feeble from being kept in the small cramped dark inside you so long. Yes, there is joy, fulfillment and companionship &#8212; but the loneliness of the soul in it’s appalling self-consciousness, is horrible and overpowering.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_62202\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/sylviaplath_smithsonian2.jpg?resize=680%2C777&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"777\" class=\"size-full wp-image-62202\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/sylviaplath_smithsonian2.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/sylviaplath_smithsonian2.jpg?resize=240%2C274&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/sylviaplath_smithsonian2.jpg?resize=320%2C366&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/sylviaplath_smithsonian2.jpg?resize=768%2C878&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/sylviaplath_smithsonian2.jpg?resize=600%2C686&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Self-Portrait, late 1940s or early 1950s &#8212; one of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/08/17/sylvia-plath-one-life-smithsonian-visual-art/\">Sylvia Plath&#8217;s little-known paintings</a>. (Smithsonian National Portrait Gallery)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>It was Plath&#8217;s tragedy that after chance had dealt her neurochemistry and nurture far from optimal, and that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/10/27/sylvia-plath-journals-privilege-free-will/\">the delicious illusion of choice</a> had led her to a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/07/16/sylvia-plath-ted-hughes-bbc-interview-1961/\">complicated love</a> that deepened her art and deepened the pain from which it sprang. But her concrete tragedy &#8212; which is a common tragedy: so often our unhealed wounds lead us to people whose claws fit those wounds and deepen them &#8212; is contoured by the luminous negative space of the opposite possibility: Some loves can unseal, irradiate, and heal those small dark old places in us where joy has been compacted into a hard dense loneliness. This possibility is folded into a glorious, maddening Möbius strip of trust: The very relationships in which we can begin to grow those twin roots of the soul require a level of trust to begin the terrifying process of being known &#8212; a process Adrienne Rich placed at the heart of every relationship in which two people have together earned the right to use the word &#8220;love,&#8221; a truly honorable relationship shaped by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/07/02/adrienne-rich-honorable-human-relationship/\">&#8220;a process, delicate, violent, often terrifying to both persons involved, a process of refining the truths they can tell each other.&#8221;</a></p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/06/sylviaplathjournals.jpg?w=680&ssl=1","linkMd5":"fd442724c766c766d2c02752ce4fe4cc","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn72@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-29-867_e49afde2f5498c15.webp","destWidth":258,"destHeight":400,"sourceBytes":10342,"destBytes":10342,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/06/sylviaplathjournals.jpg?w=680&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn72@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-29-867_e49afde2f5498c15.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/sylviapalth_smithsonian.jpg?resize=680%2C908&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-35-34-527_b4994e972af8e4f2.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/sylviaplath_smithsonian2.jpg?resize=680%2C777&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn32@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-34-790_2d65389254c7cdc1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/6XJC1TN6Wz8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn8@2020_2/2021/07/12/18-35-45-664_4538b2aa591a9b4c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114913558},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","title":"The Mirror of Enigmas: Chance, the Universe, and the Pale Blues of Knowing Who We Are","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73651","description":"<h3>&#8220;There is no human being on earth capable of declaring with certitude who he is.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Labyrinths-Directions-Paperbook-Jorge-Borges/dp/0811216993/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"516\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/borges_labyrinths-1.jpg?fit=320%2C516&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"The Mirror of Enigmas: Chance, the Universe, and the Pale Blues of Knowing Who We Are\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/borges_labyrinths-1.jpg?w=740&#38;ssl=1 740w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/borges_labyrinths-1.jpg?resize=240%2C387&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/borges_labyrinths-1.jpg?resize=320%2C516&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/borges_labyrinths-1.jpg?resize=600%2C967&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>It takes a great sobriety of spirit to know your own depths &#8212; and your limits. It takes a special grandeur of spirit to know the limits of your self-knowledge. </p>\n<p>A recent brush with those limits reminded me of a short, stunning essay by <strong>Jorge Luis Borges</strong> (August 24, 1899&#8211;June 14, 1986) titled &#8220;The Mirror of Enigmas,&#8221; found in his <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Labyrinths-Directions-Paperbook-Jorge-Borges/dp/0811216993/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Labyrinths</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/labyrinths-selected-stories-other-writings/oclc/260942&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; the 1962 collection of stories, essays, and parables that gave us his timeless <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/06/borges-and-i/\">parable of the divided self</a> and his classic <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/19/a-new-refutation-of-time-borges/\">refutation of time</a>.</p>\n<p>Titling the essay after St. Paul&#8217;s famous cryptic statement <em>Videmus nunc per speculum in aenigmate</em> &#8212; loosely translated as <em>We now see through a mirror, enigmatically</em> &#8212; Borges considers the tribe of thinkers who have perched their efforts to reconcile knowledge and mystery, the scientific and the spiritual, on the assumption that &#8220;the history of the universe &#8212; and in it our lives and the most tenuous detail of our lives &#8212; has an incalculable, symbolical value.&#8221; With his characteristic poetic precision, he condenses this common and somewhat tired hypothesis: </p>\n<blockquote><p>The outer world &#8212; forms, temperatures, the moon &#8212; is a language humans have forgotten or which we can scarcely distinguish.</p></blockquote>\n<p>No one, Borges argues, has taken this precarious hypothesis to more surefooted ground than the French novelist, poet, and philosophical pamphleteer <strong>Léon Bloy</strong> (July 11, 1846&#8211;November 3, 1917). </p>\n<p>Digging through the surviving fragments of Bloy&#8217;s written thought, he surfaces a passage emblematic of Bloy&#8217;s uncommon physics of the metaphysical &#8212; an 1894 passage fomented by his interest in the teachings of St. Paul. Translated by Borges himself, Bloy writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>[St. Paul&#8217;s statement] would be a skylight through which one might submerge himself in the true Abyss, which is the soul of man. The terrifying immensity of the firmament&#8217;s abyss is an illusion, an external reflection of <em>our own</em> abysses, perceived &#8220;in a mirror.&#8221; We should invert our eyes and practice a sublime astronomy in the infinitude of our heart&#8230; If we see the Milky Way, it is because it <em>actually exists in our souls</em>.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72737\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-1750_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=680%2C977&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"977\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72737\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=240%2C345&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=320%2C460&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=768%2C1103&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=600%2C862&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from Thomas Wright&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\"><em>An Original Theory or New Hypothesis of the Universe</em></a>, 1750 &#8212; the first book to describe the spiral shape of the Milky Way. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-1750_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>A century before Milan Kundera considered <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/10/16/milan-kundera-unbearable-lightness-of-being/\">the eternal challenge of knowing what we really want</a> in his classic novel <em>The Unbearable Lightness of Being</em>, Bloy shines a sidewise gleam on the elemental self-opacity with and within which we live:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Everything is a symbol, even the most piercing pain. We are dreamers who shout in our sleep. We do not know whether the things afflicting us are the secret beginning of our ulterior happiness or not.</p></blockquote>\n<p>These ideas haunted Bloy, animated his pamphlets, his poems, his novels, then culminated in his 1912 book-length essay <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Soul-Napoleon-Léon-Bloy/dp/1955392005/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>The Soul of Napoleon</em></a> &#8212; a philosophical prose poem that sets out, as Borges puts it, &#8220;to decipher the symbol Napoleon, considered as the precursor of another hero &#8212; man and symbol as well &#8212; who is hidden in the future.&#8221; Bloy, translated again by Borges, writes in this uncommon work:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Every man<a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/10/17/ursula-k-le-guin-gender/\">*</a> is on earth to symbolize something he is ignorant of and to realize a particle or a mountain of the invisible materials that will serve to build the City of God.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>There is no human being on earth capable of declaring with certitude who he is. No one knows what he has come into this world to do, what his acts correspond to, his sentiments, his ideas, or what his real name is, his enduring Name in the register of Light&#8230; History is an immense liturgical text where the iotas and the dots are worth no less than the entire verses or chapters, but the importance of one and the other is indeterminable and profoundly hidden.</p></blockquote>\n<p>But as you contemplate these existential immensities, you face the limits of contemplation &#8212; the limits of meaning-making in relation to elemental truth. </p>\n<p>Borges recognized this, closing the essay with by acknowledging &#8220;it is doubtful that the world has a meaning&#8230; even more doubtful that it has a double or triple meaning.&#8221; </p>\n<p>I recognized this upon sitting down in for morning meditation in my garden after a nightlong storm and watching an almost otherworldly deposit roll onto the cushion: a tiny, perfect robin egg, improbable and sorrowful in its displaced blue beauty.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73655\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/singing-only-is_print?sku=s6-20644560p4a1v1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/SingingOnlyIs_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C907&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"907\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73655\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/SingingOnlyIs_by_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/SingingOnlyIs_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C427&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/SingingOnlyIs_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C800&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/SingingOnlyIs_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C320&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/SingingOnlyIs_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C1024&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/SingingOnlyIs_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=1152%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1152w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Singing Only Is</em> by Maria Popova. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/singing-only-is_print?sku=s6-20644560p4a1v1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>I considered climbing the neighbor’s colossal tree to find the storm-shaken nest and reinstate the egg. (Perfectly, the tree is an <em>Ailanthus altissima</em>, known as “tree-of-heaven” in its native China &#8212; a migrant now rooted in Brooklyn, like me.) </p>\n<p>But then I considered this chance-event as the product of the same impartial forces that deposited the exact spermatozoid of my father’s onto my mother’s ovum at the exact moment to produce the chance-event of my particular configuration of atoms animated by this particular consciousness that just <em>is</em>, the consciousness mourning the robin that will never be. To call one expression of chance good and another bad is mere human hubris &#8212; the hubris of narrative and interpretation superimposed on an impartial universe devoid of <em>why</em>, awash in <em>is</em>. </p>\n<p>No one knows the meaning of why anything comes to be, or doesn&#8217;t. Here is this pale blue orb, dropped from the tree-of-heaven onto a tiny Brooklyn point on the face of this Pale Blue Dot, itself a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/09/a-brave-and-startling-truth-maya-angelou/\">&#8220;mote of dust suspended in a sunbeam&#8221;</a> within an immense and impartial universe, conceived in the creation myths and early scientific theories of our meaning-hungry ancestors as a great cosmic egg. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72734\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457502_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright7.jpg?resize=680%2C1033&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1033\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72734\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright7.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright7.jpg?resize=240%2C365&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright7.jpg?resize=320%2C486&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright7.jpg?resize=768%2C1167&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright7.jpg?resize=600%2C912&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\"><em>An Original Theory or New Hypothesis of the Universe</em></a>, 1750, illustrating Thomas Wright&#8217;s model of the cosmos as an egg-like structure of nested infinities. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457502_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Here I am, and here you are, and here is the robin&#8217;s egg in its near-life collision with chance. To ask for its meaning is as meaningless a question as to demand the meaning of a color or the meaning of a bird. On this particular day, at this particular moment &#8212; the only locus of aliveness we ever have &#8212; the contour of meaning comes in shades of blue, singing only <em>is</em>. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. 02:35:13","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:13","title":"The Ocean and the Meaning of Life","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=73640","description":"<h3>&#8220;Contemplating the teeming life of the shore, we have an uneasy sense of the communication of some universal truth that lies just beyond our grasp&#8230; the ultimate mystery of Life itself.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p class=\"via\"><em>This essay is adapted from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/11/01/figuring/\"><em>Figuring</em></a></em>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/11/01/figuring/\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/figuring_jacket_final.jpg\" /></a>In June of 1952, the United States Fish &#038; Wildlife Service received a letter of resignation from its most famous marine biologist. On the line requesting the reason for resignation, she had stated plainly: &#8220;To devote my time to writing.&#8221; But she was also leaving for the freedom to use her public voice as an instrument of change, awakening the world&#8217;s ecological conscience with her <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/08/rachel-carson-washington-post-letter-1953/\">bold open letters</a> holding the government accountable for its exploitation of nature. </p>\n<p>Fifteen years earlier, at age twenty-nine, <strong>Rachel Carson</strong> (May 27, 1907&#8211;April 14, 1964) had gotten her start at the lowest rungs of the government agency as a field aide hired at $6.50 an hour. Wading through tide pools and annual marine census reports as a junior aquatic biologist, she had found her voice as a writer with an uncommon gift for walking the teeming shoreline between the scientific and the poetic. In an unexampled essay that eventually bloomed into <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/08/21/rachel-carson-the-sea-around-us-blue/\"><em>The Sea Around Us</em></a>, which won her the National Book Award, she had <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/28/undersea-rachel-carson/\">invited the human imagination undersea</a>, into a world then more mysterious than the Moon. Now, forty-five and finally free from the day-job by which she had been supporting her mother, her sister, and the young nephew she adopted and raised as her son after her sister&#8217;s death, Carson set out to fulfill her childhood dream of living by the ocean. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_60151\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/rachel-carson/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/rachelcarson_undersea.jpg?resize=680%2C398&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"398\" class=\"size-full wp-image-60151\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/rachelcarson_undersea.jpg?w=850&#38;ssl=1 850w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/rachelcarson_undersea.jpg?resize=240%2C141&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/rachelcarson_undersea.jpg?resize=320%2C187&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/rachelcarson_undersea.jpg?resize=768%2C450&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/rachelcarson_undersea.jpg?resize=600%2C352&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Rachel Carson</figcaption></figure>\n<p>After searching along the New England coast, she fell in love with West Southport &#8212; a picturesque island in Maine, nestled among evergreens and oaks in the estuary of the Sheepscot River, where seals frequented the beach and whales billowed by as though torn from the pages of her beloved Melville. With her book royalties, she bought a plot of land on which to build a cottage. In a touching testament to her orientation to the natural world, she felt deeply uncomfortable thinking of herself as its &#8220;owner&#8221; &#8212; a &#8220;strange and inappropriate word&#8221; &#8212; of this &#8220;perfectly magnificent piece of Maine shoreline.” There, she would soon meet <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/13/rachel-carson-dorothy-freeman-letters/\">her soul mate</a>, whose love would bolster Carson&#8217;s moral courage in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/27/rachel-carson-silent-spring-dorothy-freeman/\">catalyzing the environmental movement</a>; there, she would compose her next book, dedicating it to her beloved Dorothy for having gone down with her &#8220;into the low-tide world&#8221; and &#8220;felt its beauty and its mystery.&#8221; </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Edge-Sea-Rachel-Carson/dp/0395924960/?tag=brainpick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>The Edge of the Sea</em></a> was an ambitious guide to the seashore &#8212; the place where Carson found &#8220;a sense of the unhurried deliberation of earth processes that move with infinite leisure, with all eternity at their disposal&#8221;; the strange and wondrous boundary the <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/16/on-the-beach-alone-at-night-walt-whitman/\">ocean-loving Whitman</a> had once extolled as “that suggesting, dividing line, contact, junction&#8230; blending the real and ideal, and each made portion of the other.” </p>\n<p>The book was also an admonition against what we stand to lose &#8212; writing in the early 1950s, Carson noted the systematically documented and “well recognized” fact of global climate change. But was primarily a celebration, for that is always the most effective instrument of admonition &#8212; a celebration of what we have and what we are, an ode to &#8220;how that marvelous, tough, vital, and adaptable something we know as LIFE has come to occupy one part of the sea world and how it has adjusted itself and survived despite the immense, blind forces acting upon it from every side.”</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73026\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-moon-at-ninomiya-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564891p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=680%2C1014&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1014\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73026\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=320%2C477&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=600%2C895&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=240%2C358&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=768%2C1146&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=1030%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1030w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Spring Moon at Ninomiya Beach</em>, 1931 &#8212; one of Hasui Kawase&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/22/hasui-kawase-prints/\">stunning vintage Japanese woodblocks</a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-moon-at-ninomiya-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564891p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Inevitably, in telling the story of life, the book takes on an existential undertone, rendered symphonic under Carson&#8217;s poetic pen. Watching the fog engulf the rocks beneath her study window as the night tide rolls in, she considers the totality of being, which the world&#8217;s oceans contour and connect:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Hearing the rising tide, I think how it is pressing also against other shores I know &#8212; rising on a southern beach where there is no fog, but a moon edging all the waves with silver and touching the wet sands with lambent sheen, and on a still more distant shore sending its streaming currents against the moonlit pinnacles and the dark caves of the coral rock. </p>\n<p>Then in my thoughts these shores, so different in their nature and in the inhabitants they support, are made one by the unifying touch of the sea. For the differences I sense in this particular instant of time that is mine are but the differences of a moment, determined by our place in the stream of time and in the long rhythms of the sea. Once this rocky coast beneath me was a plain of sand; then the sea rose and found a new shore line. And again in some shadowy future the surf will have ground these rocks to sand and will have returned the coast to its earlier state. And so in my mind’s eye these coastal forms merge and blend in a shifting, kaleidoscopic pattern in which there is no finality, no ultimate and fixed reality &#8212; earth becoming fluid as the sea itself.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73641\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-great-wave-off-kanagawa-by-hokusai-1831_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=680%2C457&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"457\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73641\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=320%2C215&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=600%2C404&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=240%2C161&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=768%2C516&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Great Wave off Kanagawa</em> by Japanese artist Hokusai, 1831. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-great-wave-off-kanagawa-by-hokusai-1831_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The year of Carson&#8217;s death, as Dorothy scattered her ashes into the rocking bay, James Baldwin would echo these existential undertones in his poetic insistence that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/21/nothing-is-fixed-james-baldwin-morley-music/\">&#8220;nothing is fixed, forever and forever and forever&#8230; the sea does not cease to grind down rock.&#8221;</a> Carson &#8212; still alive, still islanded for a mortal moment in the ocean of ongoingness &#8212; adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>On all these shores there are echoes of past and future: of the flow of time, obliterating yet containing all that has gone before; of the sea’s eternal rhythms &#8212; the tides, the beat of surf, the pressing rivers of the currents &#8212; shaping, changing, dominating; of the stream of life, flowing as inexorably as any ocean current, from past to unknown future.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>Contemplating the teeming life of the shore, we have an uneasy sense of the communication of some universal truth that lies just beyond our grasp. What is the message signaled by the hordes of diatoms, flashing their microscopic lights in the night sea? What truth is expressed by the legions of the barnacles, whitening the rocks with their habitations, each small creature within finding the necessities of its existence in the sweep of the surf? And what is the meaning of so tiny a being as the transparent wisp of protoplasm that is a sea lace, existing for some reason inscrutable to us &#8212; a reason that demands its presence by the trillion amid the rocks and weeds of the shore? The meaning haunts and ever eludes us, and in its very pursuit we approach the ultimate mystery of Life itself.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73613\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/chart-from-geographical-portfolio-by-levi-walter-yaggy-18875256960_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/yaggi_nature_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C460&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"460\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73613\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/yaggi_nature_sm.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/yaggi_nature_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C216&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/yaggi_nature_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C406&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/yaggi_nature_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C162&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/yaggi_nature_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C519&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from <em>Geographical Portfolio &#8212; Comprising Physical, Political, Geological, and Astronomical Geography</em> by Levi Walter Yaggy, 1887. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/chart-from-geographical-portfolio-by-levi-walter-yaggy-18875256960_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As <em>The Edge of the Sea</em> alighted in the world, critical praise and honors came cascading, trailed by invitations for lectures and acceptance speeches. Always uncomfortable with attention and public appearances, Carson became even more selective, prioritizing women’s associations and nonprofit cultural institutions over glamorous commercial stages. When she did speak, her words became almost a consecration, as in a speech she delivered before a convocation of librarians:</p>\n<blockquote><p>When we go down to the lowest of the low tide lines and look down into the shallow waters, there’s all the excitement of discovering a new world. Once you have entered such a world, its fascination grows and somehow you find your mind has gained a new dimension, a new perspective &#8212; and always thereafter you find yourself remember[ing] the beauty and strangeness and wonder of that world &#8212; a world that is as real, as much a part of the universe, as our own.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_62269\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/rachel-carson/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/rachelcarson_1951.jpg?resize=680%2C338&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"338\" class=\"size-full wp-image-62269\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/rachelcarson_1951.jpg?w=700&#38;ssl=1 700w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/rachelcarson_1951.jpg?resize=240%2C119&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/rachelcarson_1951.jpg?resize=320%2C159&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/rachelcarson_1951.jpg?resize=600%2C298&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Rachel Carson, 1951</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Savor more of Carson&#8217;s lyrical reverence for the sea and the strange wonder of life in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/11/01/figuring/\"><em>Figuring</em></a></em>. Couple this fragment with a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/08/29/water-subhash-vyam/\">stunning illustrated celebration of our water world</a> based on Indian mythology, then revisit Carson&#8217;s life-tested wisdom on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/08/28/rachel-carson-house-of-life-writing-loneliness/\">writing and the loneliness of creative work</a>, the story of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/27/rachel-carson-silent-spring-dorothy-freeman/\">how her writing sparked the environmental movement</a>, and Neil Gaiman&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/02/07/after-silence-neil-gaiman-rachel-carson/\">poetic tribute to her legacy</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter.
